<td colspan="2" style="text-align: center; font-size: 88%">Aardvark range
</td></tr>












</tbody></table><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1238732961">@media screen{html.skin-theme-clientpref-night .mw-parser-output .infobox.biota tr{background:transparent!important}html.skin-theme-clientpref-night .mw-parser-output .infobox.biota img{background:transparent}}@media screen and (prefers-color-scheme:dark){html.skin-theme-clientpref-os .mw-parser-output .infobox.biota tr{background:transparent!important}html.skin-theme-clientpref-os .mw-parser-output .infobox.biota img{background:white}}.mw-parser-output .infobox.biota .taxobox-edit-taxonomy img{background:transparent!important}body.skin-vector .mw-parser-output table.biota.infobox{margin-top:0.5em}body.skin--responsive .mw-parser-output table.biota.infobox tr.taxonrow td{padding:2px 10px}</style>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Aardvark_Skeleton.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Aardvark_Skeleton.jpg/220px-Aardvark_Skeleton.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Aardvark_Skeleton.jpg/330px-Aardvark_Skeleton.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Aardvark_Skeleton.jpg/440px-Aardvark_Skeleton.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456" /></a><figcaption>Skeleton of an aardvark</figcaption></figure>
<p><b>Aardvarks</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="/ɑːr/: &#39;ar&#39; in &#39;far&#39;">ɑːr</span><span title="&#39;d&#39; in &#39;dye&#39;">d</span><span title="&#39;v&#39; in &#39;vie&#39;">v</span><span title="/ɑːr/: &#39;ar&#39; in &#39;far&#39;">ɑːr</span><span title="&#39;k&#39; in &#39;kind&#39;">k</span></span>/</a></span></span> <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i title="English pronunciation respelling"><span style="font-size:90%">ARD</span>-vark</i></a>; <i><b>Orycteropus afer</b></i>) are medium-sized, burrowing, <a href="/wiki/Nocturnal" class="mw-redirect" title="Nocturnal">nocturnal</a> mammals native to Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-EB_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> They have a long snout, similar to that of a pig, which is used to sniff out food.
</p><p>Aardvarks are the only living <a href="/wiki/Species" title="Species">species</a> of the order <a href="/wiki/Tubulidentata" class="mw-redirect" title="Tubulidentata">Tubulidentata</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-MSW3_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MSW3-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-EoM_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EoM-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> although other prehistoric species and genera of Tubulidentata are known. They are <a href="/wiki/Afrothere" class="mw-redirect" title="Afrothere">afrotheres</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Clade" title="Clade">clade</a> that also includes <a href="/wiki/Elephants" class="mw-redirect" title="Elephants">elephants</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manatees" class="mw-redirect" title="Manatees">manatees</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hyraxes" class="mw-redirect" title="Hyraxes">hyraxes</a>.
</p><p>They are found over much of the southern two-thirds of the African continent, avoiding areas that are mainly rocky. Nocturnal feeders, aardvarks subsist on ants and termites by using their sharp claws and powerful legs to dig the insects out of their hills. Aardvarks also dig to create burrows in which to live and rear their young.
</p><p>Aardvarks are listed as "least concern" by the <a href="/wiki/IUCN" class="mw-redirect" title="IUCN">IUCN</a>, although their numbers are decreasing.
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Name_and_taxonomy">Name and taxonomy</h2></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Name">Name</h3></div>
<p>The aardvark is sometimes colloquially called the "African ant bear",<sup id="cite_ref-Colliers_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Colliers-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> "anteater" (not to be confused with the <a href="/wiki/Anteater" title="Anteater">South American anteaters</a>), or the "Cape anteater"<sup id="cite_ref-Colliers_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Colliers-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> after the <a href="/wiki/Cape_of_Good_Hope" title="Cape of Good Hope">Cape of Good Hope</a>.
</p><p>The name "aardvark" is <a href="/wiki/Afrikaans" title="Afrikaans">Afrikaans</a> (<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1177148991">.mw-parser-output .IPA-label-small{font-size:85%}.mw-parser-output .references .IPA-label-small,.mw-parser-output .infobox .IPA-label-small,.mw-parser-output .navbox .IPA-label-small{font-size:100%}</style><span class="IPA-label IPA-label-small">pronounced</span> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="af-Latn-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Afrikaans" title="Help:IPA/Afrikaans">&#91;ˈɑːrtfark&#93;</a></span>) and comes from earlier Afrikaans <span title="Afrikaans-language text"><i lang="af">erdvark</i></span>.<sup id="cite_ref-Colliers_6-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Colliers-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It means "earth <a href="/wiki/Pig" title="Pig">pig</a>" or "ground pig" (<span title="Afrikaans-language text"><i lang="af">aarde</i></span>: <span class="gloss-quot">'</span><span class="gloss-text">earth</span><span class="gloss-quot">'</span>, <span title="Afrikaans-language text"><i lang="af">vark</i></span>: <span class="gloss-quot">'</span><span class="gloss-text">pig, young pig</span><span class="gloss-quot">'</span>), because of its burrowing habits.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The name <i>Orycteropus</i> means "burrowing foot", and the name <i>afer</i> refers to Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-sho_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sho-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The name of the aardvark's order, <i>Tubulidentata,</i> comes from the tubule-style teeth.<sup id="cite_ref-sho1_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sho1-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Taxonomy">Taxonomy</h3></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Aardvark_skull.JPG" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Aardvark_skull.JPG/220px-Aardvark_skull.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="159" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Aardvark_skull.JPG/330px-Aardvark_skull.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Aardvark_skull.JPG/440px-Aardvark_skull.JPG 2x" data-file-width="872" data-file-height="630" /></a><figcaption>Skull of an aardvark</figcaption></figure>
<p>The aardvark is not closely related to the pig; rather, it is the sole extant representative of the obscure mammalian <a href="/wiki/Order_(biology)" title="Order (biology)">order</a> <a href="/wiki/Tubulidentata" class="mw-redirect" title="Tubulidentata">Tubulidentata</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-sho_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sho-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> in which it is usually considered to form one variable species of the genus <i><a href="/wiki/Orycteropus" title="Orycteropus">Orycteropus</a></i>, the sole surviving genus in the family <a href="/wiki/Orycteropodidae" title="Orycteropodidae">Orycteropodidae</a>. The aardvark is not closely related to the <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South American</a> <a href="/wiki/Anteater" title="Anteater">anteater</a>, despite sharing some characteristics and a superficial resemblance.<sup id="cite_ref-awf_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-awf-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The similarities are the outcome of <a href="/wiki/Convergent_evolution" title="Convergent evolution">convergent evolution</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-UR2_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UR2-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The closest living relatives of the aardvark are the <a href="/wiki/Elephant_shrew" title="Elephant shrew">elephant shrews</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tenrecidae" class="mw-redirect" title="Tenrecidae">tenrecidae</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Golden_mole" title="Golden mole">golden moles</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Along with <a href="/wiki/Sirenian" class="mw-redirect" title="Sirenian">sirenians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hyrax" title="Hyrax">hyraxes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elephant" title="Elephant">elephants</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and their extinct relatives, these animals form the superorder <a href="/wiki/Afrotheria" title="Afrotheria">Afrotheria</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-UR_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UR-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Studies of the brain have shown the similarities with <a href="/wiki/Condylarthra" title="Condylarthra">Condylarthra</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-UR2_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UR2-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Evolutionary_history">Evolutionary history</h3></div>
<p>Based on his study of fossils, <a href="/wiki/Bryan_Patterson" title="Bryan Patterson">Bryan Patterson</a> has concluded that early relatives of the aardvark appeared in <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a> around the end of the <a href="/wiki/Paleocene" title="Paleocene">Paleocene</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-UR2_13-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UR2-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sho2_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sho2-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Ptolemaiida" title="Ptolemaiida">ptolemaiidans</a>, a mysterious clade of mammals with uncertain affinities, may actually be stem-aardvarks, either as a sister clade to <a href="/wiki/Tubulidentata" class="mw-redirect" title="Tubulidentata">Tubulidentata</a> or as a grade leading to true tubulidentates.<sup id="cite_ref-Cote_et_al_2007_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cote_et_al_2007-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Seifert2007_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Seifert2007-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The first unambiguous tubulidentate was probably <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Myorycteropus_africanus&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Myorycteropus africanus (page does not exist)">Myorycteropus africanus</a></i> from <a href="/wiki/Kenya" title="Kenya">Kenyan</a> <a href="/wiki/Miocene" title="Miocene">Miocene</a> deposits.<sup id="cite_ref-UR2_13-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UR2-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The earliest example from the genus <i><a href="/wiki/Orycteropus" title="Orycteropus">Orycteropus</a></i> was <i><a href="/wiki/Amphiorycteropus" title="Amphiorycteropus">Orycteropus mauritanicus</a></i>, found in <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">Algeria</a> in deposits from the middle Miocene, with an equally old version found in Kenya.<sup id="cite_ref-UR2_13-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UR2-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Fossils from the aardvark have been dated to 5 million years, and have been located throughout <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Near_East" title="Near East">Near East</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-UR2_13-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UR2-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The mysterious Pleistocene <i><a href="/wiki/Plesiorycteropus" title="Plesiorycteropus">Plesiorycteropus</a></i> from <a href="/wiki/Madagascar" title="Madagascar">Madagascar</a> was originally thought to be a tubulidentate that was descended from ancestors that entered the island during the <a href="/wiki/Eocene" title="Eocene">Eocene</a>. However, a number of subtle anatomical differences coupled with recent molecular evidence now lead researchers to believe that <i>Plesiorycteropus</i> is a relative of golden moles and <a href="/wiki/Tenrec" title="Tenrec">tenrecs</a> that achieved an aardvark-like appearance and ecological niche through convergent evolution.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Subspecies">Subspecies</h3></div>
<p>The aardvark has seventeen poorly defined subspecies listed:<sup id="cite_ref-MSW3_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MSW3-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orycteropus_afer_afer&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Orycteropus afer afer (page does not exist)">Orycteropus afer afer</a></i> (Southern aardvark)</li>
<li><i>O. a. adametzi</i> <small> Grote, 1921</small> (Western aardvark)</li>
<li><i>O. a. aethiopicus</i> <small> <a href="/wiki/Carl_Jakob_Sundevall" title="Carl Jakob Sundevall">Sundevall</a>, 1843</small></li>
<li><i>O. a. angolensis</i> <small> Zukowsky &amp; <a href="/wiki/Theodor_Haltenorth" title="Theodor Haltenorth">Haltenorth</a>, 1957</small></li>
<li><i>O. a. erikssoni</i> <small> <a href="/wiki/Einar_L%C3%B6nnberg" title="Einar Lönnberg">Lönnberg</a>, 1906</small></li>
<li><i>O. a. faradjius</i> <small> Hatt, 1932</small></li>
<li><i>O. a. haussanus</i> <small> <a href="/wiki/Paul_Matschie" title="Paul Matschie">Matschie</a>, 1900</small></li>
<li><i>O. a. kordofanicus</i> <small> <a href="/wiki/Walter_Rothschild,_2nd_Baron_Rothschild" title="Walter Rothschild, 2nd Baron Rothschild">Rothschild</a>, 1927</small></li>
<li><i>O. a. lademanni</i> <small> Grote, 1911</small></li>
<li><i>O. a. leptodon</i> <small> Hirst, 1906</small></li>
<li><i>O. a. matschiei</i> <small> Grote, 1921</small></li>
<li><i>O. a. observandus</i> <small>Grote, 1921</small></li>
<li><i>O. a. ruvanensis</i> <small>Grote, 1921</small></li>
<li><i>O. a. senegalensis</i> <small><a href="/wiki/Ren%C3%A9_Primev%C3%A8re_Lesson" class="mw-redirect" title="René Primevère Lesson">Lesson</a>, 1840</small></li>
<li><i>O. a. somalicus</i> <small><a href="/wiki/Richard_Lydekker" title="Richard Lydekker">Lydekker</a>, 1908</small></li>
<li><i>O. a. wardi</i> <small>Lydekker, 1908</small></li>
<li><i>O. a. wertheri</i> <small> Matschie, 1898</small> (Eastern aardvark)</li></ul>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/1911_Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica" class="mw-redirect" title="1911 Encyclopædia Britannica">1911 Encyclopædia Britannica</a> also mentions <i>O.&#160;a. capensis</i> or Cape ant-bear from South Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Description">Description</h2></div>

tmulti tleft"><div class="thumbinner multiimageinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Orycteropus_afer_175359476.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Orycteropus_afer_175359476.jpg/200px-Orycteropus_afer_175359476.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="289" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Orycteropus_afer_175359476.jpg/300px-Orycteropus_afer_175359476.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Orycteropus_afer_175359476.jpg/400px-Orycteropus_afer_175359476.jpg 2x" data-file-width="420" data-file-height="607" /></a></span></div></div></div><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Southern_Aardvark_foot_print.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Southern_Aardvark_foot_print.jpg/200px-Southern_Aardvark_foot_print.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="133" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Southern_Aardvark_foot_print.jpg/300px-Southern_Aardvark_foot_print.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Southern_Aardvark_foot_print.jpg/400px-Southern_Aardvark_foot_print.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1365" /></a></span></div><div class="thumbcaption">Southern aardvark (<i>O.<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>a. afer</i>) front and rear foot print</div></div></div></div></div><p>
The aardvark is vaguely pig-like in appearance. Its body is stout with a prominently arched back<sup id="cite_ref-UR1_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UR1-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and is sparsely covered with coarse hairs. The limbs are of moderate length, with the rear legs being longer than the forelegs.<sup id="cite_ref-UR_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UR-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The front feet have lost the pollex (or 'thumb'), resulting in four toes, while the rear feet have all five toes. Each toe bears a large, robust <a href="/wiki/Nail_(anatomy)" title="Nail (anatomy)">nail</a> which is somewhat flattened and shovel-like, and appears to be intermediate between a <a href="/wiki/Claw" title="Claw">claw</a> and a hoof. Whereas the aardvark is considered <a href="/wiki/Digitigrade" title="Digitigrade">digitigrade</a>, it appears at times to be <a href="/wiki/Plantigrade" title="Plantigrade">plantigrade</a>. This confusion happens because when it squats it stands on its soles.<sup id="cite_ref-UR1_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UR1-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A contributing characteristic to the burrow digging capabilities of aardvarks is an endosteal tissue called compacted coarse cancellous bone (CCCB). The stress and strain resistance provided by CCCB allows aardvarks to create their burrows, ultimately leading to a favourable environment for plants and a variety of animals.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></p><figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Aardvark_skeleton_mount.JPG" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Aardvark_skeleton_mount.JPG/220px-Aardvark_skeleton_mount.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="293" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Aardvark_skeleton_mount.JPG/330px-Aardvark_skeleton_mount.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Aardvark_skeleton_mount.JPG/440px-Aardvark_skeleton_mount.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2304" data-file-height="3072" /></a><figcaption>An aardvark skeleton and mounted individual</figcaption></figure><p>An aardvark's weight is typically between 60 and 80 kilograms (130–180&#160;lb).<sup id="cite_ref-UR_16-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UR-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> An aardvark's length is usually between 105 and 130 centimetres (3.44–4.27&#160;ft),<sup id="cite_ref-EoM_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EoM-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and can reach lengths of 2.2 metres (7&#160;ft 3&#160;in) when its tail (which can be up to 70 centimetres (28&#160;in)) is taken into account. It is 60 centimetres (24&#160;in) tall at the shoulder, and has a girth of about 100 centimetres (3.3&#160;ft).<sup id="cite_ref-UR1_22-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UR1-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It is the <a href="/wiki/Largest_organisms" title="Largest organisms">largest</a> member of the proposed clade <a href="/wiki/Afroinsectiphilia" title="Afroinsectiphilia">Afroinsectiphilia</a>. The aardvark is pale yellowish-grey in colour and often stained reddish-brown by <a href="/wiki/Soil" title="Soil">soil</a>. The aardvark's coat is thin, and the animal's primary protection is its tough skin. Its hair is short on its head and tail; however its legs tend to have longer hair.<sup id="cite_ref-EoM_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EoM-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The hair on the majority of its body is grouped in clusters of 3–4 hairs.<sup id="cite_ref-UR1_22-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UR1-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The hair surrounding its nostrils is dense to help filter particulate matter out as it digs. Its tail is very thick at the base and gradually tapers.
</p><div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Head">Head</h3></div>
<p>The greatly elongated head is set on a short, thick neck, and the end of the snout bears a disc, which houses the nostrils. It contains a thin but complete <a href="/wiki/Zygomatic_arch" title="Zygomatic arch">zygomatic arch</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-UR1_22-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UR1-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The head of the aardvark contains many unique and different features. One of the most distinctive characteristics of the Tubulidentata is their <a href="/wiki/Tooth" title="Tooth">teeth</a>. Instead of having a <a href="/wiki/Pulp_(tooth)" title="Pulp (tooth)">pulp cavity</a>, each tooth has a cluster of thin, hexagonal, upright, parallel tubes of vasodentin (a modified form of <a href="/wiki/Dentine" class="mw-redirect" title="Dentine">dentine</a>), with individual pulp canals, held together by <a href="/wiki/Cementum" title="Cementum">cementum</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-UR_16-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UR-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The number of columns is dependent on the size of the tooth, with the largest having about 1,500.<sup id="cite_ref-UR2_13-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UR2-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The teeth have no <a href="/wiki/Tooth_enamel" title="Tooth enamel">enamel</a> coating and are worn away and regrow continuously.<sup id="cite_ref-sho1_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sho1-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The aardvark is born with conventional incisors and <a href="/wiki/Canine_tooth" title="Canine tooth">canines</a> at the front of the jaw, which fall out and are not replaced. Adult aardvarks have only cheek teeth at the back of the <a href="/wiki/Jaw" title="Jaw">jaw</a>, and have a <a href="/wiki/Dentition" title="Dentition">dental formula</a> of: <span class="nowrap"><span style="display:inline-block; vertical-align:-0.5em; font-size:85%; text-align:center;"><span style="display:block; line-height:1em; padding:0 0.1em;" title="upper dentition: Incisors.Canines.Premolars.Molars">0.0.2-3.3</span><span style="display:block; line-height:1em; padding:0 0.1em; border-top:1px solid;" title="lower dentition: Incisors.Canines.Premolars.Molars">0.0.2.3</span></span></span> These remaining teeth are peg-like and rootless and are of unique composition.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The teeth consist of 14 upper and 12 lower jaw molars.<sup id="cite_ref-Colliers_6-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Colliers-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The nasal area of the aardvark is another unique area, as it contains ten <a href="/wiki/Nasal_concha" title="Nasal concha">nasal conchae</a>, more than any other placental mammal.<sup id="cite_ref-UR_16-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UR-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The sides of the nostrils are thick with hair.<sup id="cite_ref-UR1_22-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UR1-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The tip of the snout is highly mobile and is moved by modified <a href="/wiki/Mimetic_muscles" class="mw-redirect" title="Mimetic muscles">mimetic muscles</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-UR_16-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UR-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The fleshy dividing tissue between its nostrils probably has sensory functions,<sup id="cite_ref-EoM_5-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EoM-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> but it is uncertain whether they are olfactory or vibratory in nature.<sup id="cite_ref-UR6_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UR6-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Its nose is made up of more <a href="/wiki/Turbinate" class="mw-redirect" title="Turbinate">turbinate</a> bones than any other mammal, with between 9 and 11, compared to dogs with 4 to 5.<sup id="cite_ref-sho1_11-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sho1-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> With a large quantity of turbinate bones, the aardvark has more space for the moist <a href="/wiki/Epithelium" title="Epithelium">epithelium</a>, which is the location of the olfactory bulb.<sup id="cite_ref-sho1_11-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sho1-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The nose contains nine <a href="/wiki/Olfactory_bulb" title="Olfactory bulb">olfactory bulbs</a>, more than any other mammal.<sup id="cite_ref-UR1_22-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UR1-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Its keen sense of smell is not just from the quantity of bulbs in the nose but also in the development of the brain, as its <a href="/wiki/Olfactory_bulb" title="Olfactory bulb">olfactory lobe</a> is very developed.<sup id="cite_ref-UR2_13-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UR2-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The snout resembles an elongated pig snout. The mouth is small and tubular, typical of species that feed on <a href="/wiki/Ant" title="Ant">ants</a> and <a href="/wiki/Termite" title="Termite">termites</a>. The aardvark has a long, thin, snakelike, protruding tongue (as much as 30 centimetres (12&#160;in) long)<sup id="cite_ref-Colliers_6-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Colliers-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and elaborate structures supporting a keen <a href="/wiki/Olfaction" class="mw-redirect" title="Olfaction">sense of smell</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-TaylorSkinner_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TaylorSkinner-27"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The ears, which are very effective,<sup id="cite_ref-Colliers_6-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Colliers-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> are disproportionately long, about 20–25 centimetres (7.9–9.8&#160;in) long.<sup id="cite_ref-UR1_22-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UR1-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The eyes are small for its head, and consist only of <a href="/wiki/Rod_cell" title="Rod cell">rods</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-UR1_22-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UR1-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Digestive_system">Digestive system</h3></div>
<p>The aardvark's stomach has a muscular <a href="/wiki/Pyloric" class="mw-redirect" title="Pyloric">pyloric</a> area that acts as a <a href="/wiki/Gizzard" title="Gizzard">gizzard</a> to grind swallowed food up, thereby rendering chewing unnecessary.<sup id="cite_ref-EoM_5-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EoM-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Its <a href="/wiki/Cecum" title="Cecum">cecum</a> is large.<sup id="cite_ref-UR_16-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UR-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Both sexes emit a strong smelling secretion from an anal gland.<sup id="cite_ref-EoM_5-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EoM-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Its <a href="/wiki/Salivary_gland" title="Salivary gland">salivary glands</a> are highly developed and almost completely ring the neck;<sup id="cite_ref-UR_16-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UR-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> their output is what causes the tongue to maintain its tackiness.<sup id="cite_ref-UR1_22-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UR1-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The female has two pairs of <a href="/wiki/Teat" title="Teat">teats</a> in the inguinal region.<sup id="cite_ref-UR_16-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UR-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Gene" title="Gene">Genetically</a> speaking, the aardvark is a <a href="/wiki/Living_fossil" title="Living fossil">living fossil</a>, as its <a href="/wiki/Chromosome" title="Chromosome">chromosomes</a> are highly conserved, reflecting much of the early <a href="/wiki/Eutherian" class="mw-redirect" title="Eutherian">eutherian</a> arrangement before the divergence of the major modern <a href="/wiki/Taxon" title="Taxon">taxa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>28<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Habitat_and_range">Habitat and range</h2></div>
<p>Aardvarks are found in <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">sub-Saharan Africa</a>, where suitable <a href="/wiki/Habitat" title="Habitat">habitat</a> (<a href="/wiki/Savanna" title="Savanna">savannas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grassland" title="Grassland">grasslands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Woodland" title="Woodland">woodlands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bushland" title="Bushland">bushland</a>) and food (i.e., <a href="/wiki/Ants" class="mw-redirect" title="Ants">ants</a> and <a href="/wiki/Termites" class="mw-redirect" title="Termites">termites</a>) is available.<sup id="cite_ref-awf_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-awf-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> They spend the daylight hours in dark burrows to avoid the heat of the day.<sup id="cite_ref-ez_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ez-29"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The only major habitat that they are not present in is swamp forest, as the high water table precludes digging to a sufficient depth.<sup id="cite_ref-iucn_status_12_November_2021_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iucn_status_12_November_2021-1"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>1<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> They also avoid terrain rocky enough to cause problems with digging.<sup id="cite_ref-UR3_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UR3-30"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>30<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> They have been documented as high as 3,200 metres (10,500&#160;ft) in Ethiopia. They are present throughout sub-Saharan Africa all the way to South Africa with few exceptions including the coastal areas of <a href="/wiki/Namibia" title="Namibia">Namibia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ivory_Coast" title="Ivory Coast">Ivory Coast</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ghana" title="Ghana">Ghana</a>. They are not found in Madagascar.<sup id="cite_ref-iucn_status_12_November_2021_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iucn_status_12_November_2021-1"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>1<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Ecology_and_behaviour">Ecology and behaviour</h2></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Orycteropus_afer.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Orycteropus_afer.jpg/170px-Orycteropus_afer.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="170" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Orycteropus_afer.jpg/255px-Orycteropus_afer.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Orycteropus_afer.jpg/340px-Orycteropus_afer.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="1000" /></a><figcaption>Aardvark resting</figcaption></figure>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Erdvarkgat,_Dingaanstat.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Erdvarkgat%2C_Dingaanstat.jpg/220px-Erdvarkgat%2C_Dingaanstat.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Erdvarkgat%2C_Dingaanstat.jpg/330px-Erdvarkgat%2C_Dingaanstat.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Erdvarkgat%2C_Dingaanstat.jpg/440px-Erdvarkgat%2C_Dingaanstat.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="3000" /></a><figcaption>Entrance to a burrow</figcaption></figure>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:SanWild17.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/SanWild17.jpg/220px-SanWild17.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="156" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/SanWild17.jpg/330px-SanWild17.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/SanWild17.jpg/440px-SanWild17.jpg 2x" data-file-width="960" data-file-height="681" /></a><figcaption>Emerging from a burrow</figcaption></figure>
<p>Aardvarks live for up to 23&#160;years in <a href="/wiki/Captivity_(animal)" title="Captivity (animal)">captivity</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-UR_16-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UR-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Its keen hearing warns it of predators: <a href="/wiki/Lion" title="Lion">lions</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leopard" title="Leopard">leopards</a>, cheetahs, <a href="/wiki/African_wild_dog" title="African wild dog">African wild dogs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hyena" title="Hyena">hyenas</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Pythonidae" title="Pythonidae">pythons</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Colliers_6-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Colliers-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UR6_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UR6-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Some humans also hunt aardvarks for meat.<sup id="cite_ref-Colliers_6-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Colliers-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Aardvarks can dig fast or run in zigzag fashion to elude enemies, but if all else fails, they will strike with their claws, tail and shoulders, sometimes flipping onto their backs lying motionless except to lash out with all four feet.<sup id="cite_ref-UR6_26-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UR6-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> They are capable of causing substantial damage to unprotected areas of an attacker.<sup id="cite_ref-sho1_11-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sho1-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> They will also dig to escape as they can. Sometimes, when pressed, aardvarks can dig extremely quickly.<sup id="cite_ref-UR6_26-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UR6-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Feeding">Feeding</h3></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Southern_Aardvark_1.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Southern_Aardvark_1.jpg/220px-Southern_Aardvark_1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Southern_Aardvark_1.jpg/330px-Southern_Aardvark_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Southern_Aardvark_1.jpg/440px-Southern_Aardvark_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a><figcaption>The unusual cross-walk gait of the aardvark</figcaption></figure>
<p>The aardvark is <a href="/wiki/Nocturnal" class="mw-redirect" title="Nocturnal">nocturnal</a> and is a solitary creature that feeds almost exclusively on <a href="/wiki/Ant" title="Ant">ants</a> and <a href="/wiki/Termite" title="Termite">termites</a> (<a href="/wiki/Myrmecophagy" title="Myrmecophagy">myrmecophagy</a>);<sup id="cite_ref-EoM_5-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EoM-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> the only fruit eaten by aardvarks is the <a href="/wiki/Aardvark_cucumber" class="mw-redirect" title="Aardvark cucumber">aardvark cucumber</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-UR6_26-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UR6-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In fact, the cucumber and the aardvark have a symbiotic relationship as they eat the subterranean fruit, then defecate the seeds near their burrows, which then grow rapidly due to the loose soil and fertile nature of the area. The time spent in the intestine of the aardvark helps the fertility of the seed, and the fruit provides needed moisture for the aardvark.<sup id="cite_ref-sho1_11-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sho1-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UR6_26-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UR6-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> They avoid eating the African <a href="/wiki/Driver_ant" class="mw-redirect" title="Driver ant">driver ant</a> and red ants.<sup id="cite_ref-UR4_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UR4-31"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>31<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Due to their stringent diet requirements, they require a large range to survive.<sup id="cite_ref-UR3_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UR3-30"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>30<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> An aardvark emerges from its burrow in the late afternoon or shortly after sunset, and forages over a considerable home range encompassing 10 to 30 kilometres (6.2 to 18.6&#160;mi). While foraging for food, the aardvark will keep its nose to the ground and its ears pointed forward, which indicates that both smell and hearing are involved in the search for food. They zig-zag as they forage and will usually not repeat a route for 5–8 days as they appear to allow time for the termite nests to recover before feeding on it again.<sup id="cite_ref-UR4_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UR4-31"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>31<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>During a foraging period, they will stop to dig a V-shaped trench with their forefeet and then sniff it profusely as a means to explore their location.<sup id="cite_ref-EoM_5-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EoM-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> When a concentration of ants or termites is detected, the aardvark digs into it with its powerful front legs, keeping its long ears upright to listen for predators, and takes up an astonishing number of <a href="/wiki/Insect" title="Insect">insects</a> with its long, sticky tongue—as many as 50,000 in one night have been recorded. Its claws enable it to dig through the extremely hard crust of a termite or ant mound quickly. It avoids inhaling the dust by sealing the nostrils.<sup id="cite_ref-ez_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ez-29"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> When successful, the aardvark's long (up to 30 centimetres (12&#160;in))<sup id="cite_ref-EB_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> tongue licks up the insects; the termites' biting, or the ants' stinging attacks are rendered futile by the tough skin. After an aardvark visit at a termite mound, other animals will visit to pick up all the leftovers.<sup id="cite_ref-UR5_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UR5-32"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>32<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Termite mounds alone do not provide enough food for the aardvark, so they look for termites that are on the move. When these insects move, they can form columns 10–40 metres (33–131&#160;ft) long and these tend to provide easy pickings with little effort exerted by the aardvark. These columns are more common in areas of livestock or other hoofed animals.<sup id="cite_ref-UR5_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UR5-32"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>32<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The trampled grass and dung attract termites from the <i><a href="/wiki/Odontotermes" title="Odontotermes">Odontotermes</a></i>, <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microtermes&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Microtermes (page does not exist)">Microtermes</a></i>, and <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pseudacanthotermes&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Pseudacanthotermes (page does not exist)">Pseudacanthotermes</a></i> genera.<sup id="cite_ref-UR5_32-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UR5-32"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>32<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>On a nightly basis they tend to be more active during the first portion of night (roughly the four hours between 8:00<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>p.m. and 12:00<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>a.m.); however, they do not seem to prefer bright or dark nights over the other. During adverse weather or if disturbed they will retreat to their burrow systems. They cover between 2 and 5 kilometres (1.2 and 3.1&#160;mi) per night; however, some studies have shown that they may traverse as far as 30 kilometres (19&#160;mi) in a night.<sup id="cite_ref-EoM_5-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EoM-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Aardvarks shift their circadian rhythms to more diurnal activity patterns in response to a reduced food supply. This survival tactic may signify an increased risk of imminent mortality.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Vocalisation">Vocalisation</h3></div>
<p>The aardvark is a rather quiet animal. However, it does make soft grunting sounds as it forages and loud grunts as it makes for its tunnel entrance.<sup id="cite_ref-UR3_30-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UR3-30"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>30<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It makes a bleating sound if frightened.<sup id="cite_ref-UR4_31-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UR4-31"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>31<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> When it is threatened it will make for one of its burrows. If one is not close it will dig a new one rapidly. This new one will be short and require the aardvark to back out when the coast is clear.<sup id="cite_ref-UR4_31-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UR4-31"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>31<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Movement">Movement</h3></div>
<p>The aardvark is known to be a good swimmer and has been witnessed successfully swimming in strong currents.<sup id="cite_ref-UR4_31-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UR4-31"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>31<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It can dig a yard of tunnel in about five minutes,<sup id="cite_ref-UR3_30-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UR3-30"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>30<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> but otherwise moves fairly slowly.
</p><p>When leaving the burrow at night, they pause at the entrance for about ten minutes, sniffing and listening. After this period of watchfulness, it will bound out and within seconds it will be 10 metres (33&#160;ft) away. It will then pause, prick its ears, twisting its head to listen, then jump and move off to start foraging.<sup id="cite_ref-UR3_30-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UR3-30"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>30<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Aside from digging out ants and termites, the aardvark also <a href="/wiki/Fossorial" title="Fossorial">excavates</a> burrows in which to live, which generally fall into one of three categories: burrows made while foraging, refuge and resting location, and permanent homes.<sup id="cite_ref-EoM_5-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EoM-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Temporary sites are scattered around the home range and are used as refuges, while the main <a href="/wiki/Burrow" title="Burrow">burrow</a> is also used for breeding. Main burrows can be deep and extensive, have several entrances and can be as long as 13 metres (43&#160;ft).<sup id="cite_ref-EoM_5-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EoM-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> These burrows can be large enough for a person to enter.<sup id="cite_ref-Colliers_6-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Colliers-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The aardvark changes the layout of its home burrow regularly, and periodically moves on and makes a new one. The old burrows are an important part of the African wildlife scene. As they are vacated, then they are inhabited by smaller animals like the <a href="/wiki/African_Wild_Dog" class="mw-redirect" title="African Wild Dog">African wild dog</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ant-eating_chat" title="Ant-eating chat">ant-eating chat</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Nycteris_thebaica" class="mw-redirect" title="Nycteris thebaica">Nycteris thebaica</a></i> and <a href="/wiki/Warthog" title="Warthog">warthogs</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-UR4_31-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UR4-31"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>31<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Other animals that use them are hares, mongooses, hyenas, owls, pythons, and lizards. Without these refuges many animals would die during wildfire season.<sup id="cite_ref-UR4_31-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UR4-31"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>31<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Only mothers and young share burrows; however, the aardvark is known to live in small family groups or as a solitary creature.<sup id="cite_ref-Colliers_6-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Colliers-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> If attacked in the tunnel, it will escape by digging out of the tunnel thereby placing the fresh fill between it and its predator, or if it decides to fight it will roll onto its back, and attack with its claws.<sup id="cite_ref-Colliers_6-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Colliers-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The aardvark has been known to sleep in a recently excavated <a href="/wiki/Ant" title="Ant">ant</a> nest, which also serves as protection from its <a href="/wiki/Predator" class="mw-redirect" title="Predator">predators</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>34<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Reproduction">Reproduction</h3></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Aardvarks.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Aardvarks.jpg/220px-Aardvarks.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Aardvarks.jpg/330px-Aardvarks.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Aardvarks.jpg/440px-Aardvarks.jpg 2x" data-file-width="599" data-file-height="399" /></a><figcaption>Aardvark mother and young</figcaption></figure>
<p>Aardvarks pair only during the breeding season; after a <a href="/wiki/Gestation" title="Gestation">gestation</a> period of seven months,<sup id="cite_ref-EoM_5-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EoM-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> one cub weighing around 1.7–1.9 kilograms (3.7–4.2&#160;lb)<sup id="cite_ref-UR_16-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UR-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> is born during May–July.<sup id="cite_ref-Colliers_6-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Colliers-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> When born, the young has flaccid ears and many wrinkles. When nursing, it will nurse off each teat in succession.<sup id="cite_ref-UR6_26-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UR6-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> After two weeks, the folds of skin disappear and after three, the ears can be held upright.<sup id="cite_ref-UR6_26-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UR6-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> After 5–6 weeks, body hair starts growing.<sup id="cite_ref-UR6_26-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UR6-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It is able to leave the burrow to accompany its mother after only two weeks and eats termites at 9&#160;weeks,<sup id="cite_ref-UR6_26-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UR6-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and is weaned between three months<sup id="cite_ref-UR_16-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UR-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and 16&#160;weeks.<sup id="cite_ref-EoM_5-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EoM-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> At six months of age, it is able to dig its own burrows, but it will often remain with the mother until the next <a href="/wiki/Mating_season" class="mw-redirect" title="Mating season">mating season</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-EoM_5-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EoM-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and is sexually mature from approximately two years of age.<sup id="cite_ref-UR_16-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UR-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Conservation">Conservation</h2></div>
<p>Aardvarks were thought to have declining numbers,<sup id="cite_ref-Colliers_6-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Colliers-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> however, this is possibly because they are not readily seen.<sup id="cite_ref-iucn_status_12_November_2021_1-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iucn_status_12_November_2021-1"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>1<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> There are no definitive counts because of their nocturnal and secretive habits; however, their numbers seem to be stable overall. They are not considered common anywhere in Africa, but due to their large range, they maintain sufficient numbers. There may be a slight decrease in numbers in eastern, northern, and western Africa. Southern African numbers are not decreasing. It has received an official designation from the IUCN as <a href="/wiki/Least_concern" class="mw-redirect" title="Least concern">least concern</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-iucn_status_12_November_2021_1-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iucn_status_12_November_2021-1"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>1<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> However, they are a species in a precarious situation, as they are so dependent on such specific food; therefore if a problem arises with the abundance of termites, the species as a whole would be affected drastically.<sup id="cite_ref-EoM_5-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EoM-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Recent research suggests that aardvarks may be particularly vulnerable to alterations in temperature caused by climate change. <a href="/wiki/Drought" title="Drought">Droughts</a> negatively impact the availability of termites and ants, which comprise the bulk of an aardvark's diet.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>35<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>&#160;Nocturnal species faced with resource scarcity may increase their diurnal activity to spare the energy costs of staying warm at night, but this comes at the cost of withstanding high temperatures during the day. A study on aardvarks in the <a href="/wiki/Kalahari_Desert" title="Kalahari Desert">Kalahari Desert</a> saw that five out of six aardvarks being studied perished following a drought.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>36<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Aardvarks that survive droughts can take long periods of time to regain health and optimal thermoregulatory physiology, reducing the reproductive potential of the species.
</p><p>Aardvarks handle captivity well. The first zoo to have one was <a href="/wiki/London_Zoo" title="London Zoo">London Zoo</a> in 1869, which had an animal from <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-UR6_26-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UR6-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>

<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:AFR_F-111_air_to_air_refueling.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/AFR_F-111_air_to_air_refueling.jpg/200px-AFR_F-111_air_to_air_refueling.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="135" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/AFR_F-111_air_to_air_refueling.jpg/300px-AFR_F-111_air_to_air_refueling.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/AFR_F-111_air_to_air_refueling.jpg/400px-AFR_F-111_air_to_air_refueling.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1306" data-file-height="883" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/General_Dynamics_F-111_Aardvark" title="General Dynamics F-111 Aardvark">F-111 Aardvark</a></figcaption></figure>
<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:F-14A_Tomcat_of_VF-114_in_flight_1977.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/F-14A_Tomcat_of_VF-114_in_flight_1977.jpg/200px-F-14A_Tomcat_of_VF-114_in_flight_1977.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="100" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/F-14A_Tomcat_of_VF-114_in_flight_1977.jpg/300px-F-14A_Tomcat_of_VF-114_in_flight_1977.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/F-14A_Tomcat_of_VF-114_in_flight_1977.jpg/400px-F-14A_Tomcat_of_VF-114_in_flight_1977.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2818" data-file-height="1414" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/F-14_Tomcat" class="mw-redirect" title="F-14 Tomcat">F-14 Tomcat</a> from VF-114 Aardvarks with the squadron mascot painted on the tail</figcaption></figure>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/African_folklore" class="mw-redirect" title="African folklore">African folklore</a>, the aardvark is much admired because of its diligent quest for food and its fearless response to <a href="/wiki/Army_ant" title="Army ant">soldier ants</a>. <a href="/wiki/Hausa_people" title="Hausa people">Hausa</a> magicians make a charm from the heart, skin, forehead, and nails of the aardvark, which they then proceed to pound together with the root of a certain tree. Wrapped in a piece of skin and worn on the chest, the charm is said to give the owner the ability to pass through walls or roofs at night. The charm is said to be used by burglars and those seeking to visit young girls without their parents' permission.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>37<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Also, some tribes, such as the <a href="/wiki/Mangbetu_people" title="Mangbetu people">Margbetu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ayanda" title="Ayanda">Ayanda</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Logo_people" title="Logo people">Logo</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-EoM_5-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EoM-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> will use aardvark teeth to make bracelets, which are regarded as good luck charms.<sup id="cite_ref-Colliers_6-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Colliers-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The meat, which has a resemblance to pork, is eaten in certain cultures.<sup id="cite_ref-EoM_5-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EoM-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In the mythology of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Dagbon" title="Kingdom of Dagbon">Dagbon</a> people of Ghana, the aardvark is believed to possess superpowers.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>38<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Dagomba_people" title="Dagomba people">Dagombas</a> believe this animal can transfigure into and interact with humans.
</p><p>The ancient <a href="/wiki/Egyptian_mythology" title="Egyptian mythology">Egyptian god</a> <a href="/wiki/Set_(mythology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Set (mythology)">Set</a> is usually depicted with the head of an <a href="/wiki/Set_animal" title="Set animal">unidentified animal</a>, whose similarity to an aardvark has been noted in scholarship.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>39<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Read" title="Arthur Read">titular character</a> and his families from <i><a href="/wiki/Arthur_(TV_series)" title="Arthur (TV series)">Arthur</a></i>, an animated television series for children based on a book series and produced by <a href="/wiki/WGBH-TV" title="WGBH-TV">WGBH</a>, shown in more than 180 countries, is an aardvark.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>40<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In the first book of the series, <i>Arthur's Nose</i> (1976), he has a long, aardvark-like nose,<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>41<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> but in later books, his face becomes more rounded.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>42<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Otis_the_Aardvark" title="Otis the Aardvark">Otis the Aardvark</a> was a puppet character used on <a href="/wiki/Children%27s_BBC" class="mw-redirect" title="Children&#39;s BBC">Children's BBC</a> programming.
</p><p>An aardvark features as the antagonist in the cartoon <i><a href="/wiki/The_Ant_and_the_Aardvark" title="The Ant and the Aardvark">The Ant and the Aardvark</a></i> as well as in the Canadian animated series <i><a href="/wiki/The_Raccoons" title="The Raccoons">The Raccoons</a></i>.
</p><p>The supersonic fighter-bomber <a href="/wiki/General_Dynamics_F-111_Aardvark" title="General Dynamics F-111 Aardvark">F-111/FB-111</a> was nicknamed the Aardvark because of its long nose resembling the animal. It also had similarities with its nocturnal missions flown at a very low level employing ordnance that could penetrate deep into the ground. In the US Navy, the squadron <a href="/wiki/VF-114" title="VF-114">VF-114</a> was nicknamed the Aardvarks, flying <a href="/wiki/McDonnell_Douglas_F-4_Phantom_II" title="McDonnell Douglas F-4 Phantom II">F-4s</a> and then <a href="/wiki/Grumman_F-14_Tomcat" title="Grumman F-14 Tomcat">F-14s</a>. The squadron mascot was adapted from the animal in the comic strip <i><a href="/wiki/B.C._(comic_strip)#Animals_and_other_non-human_characters" title="B.C. (comic strip)">B.C.</a></i>, which the F-4 was said to resemble.
</p><p><i><a href="/wiki/Cerebus_the_Aardvark" title="Cerebus the Aardvark">Cerebus the Aardvark</a></i> is a 300-issue comic book series by Dave Sim.
</p>
